# Changelog

All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.

The English section comes first, followed by a Japanese translation.
The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/), and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

## English

### [Unreleased]

#### Added
- **T-SQL / SQL Server DDL kinds now surface as symbols (#230)** — The `SymbolExtractor` SQL row previously only captured `CREATE TABLE` / `(MATERIALIZED) VIEW` / `PROCEDURE` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` / `TYPE` / `SCHEMA` / `SEQUENCE` / `DOMAIN` / `EXTENSION` / `INDEX` and `ALTER TABLE`, so on T-SQL / SQL Server migration scripts the short-form `CREATE PROC`, T-SQL `CREATE OR ALTER` (SQL Server 2016+), `CREATE SYNONYM`, `CREATE DATABASE` / `LOGIN` / `USER` / `ROLE` / `CERTIFICATE`, `CREATE PARTITION FUNCTION` / `PARTITION SCHEME`, `CREATE FULLTEXT CATALOG`, and every non-`TABLE` `ALTER` form (procedures, views, sequences, synonyms, principals, etc.) were silently dropped from the index — making `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` / `inspect` look near-empty on enterprise .NET backends whose primary surface is a stored-procedure or schema-migration repo. The TABLE/VIEW and PROCEDURE/PROC/FUNCTION/TRIGGER rows now accept `CREATE OR (REPLACE|ALTER)`, the procedure row accepts the `PROC` synonym, dedicated rows were added for `CREATE SYNONYM` (class), `CREATE DATABASE|LOGIN|USER|ROLE|CERTIFICATE` (class), `CREATE PARTITION FUNCTION` (function) / `CREATE PARTITION SCHEME` (class), `CREATE FULLTEXT CATALOG` (class), and the `ALTER` side is split into kind-consistent rows so procedure-like `ALTER` (`PROCEDURE` / `PROC` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` / `PARTITION FUNCTION`) emits kind `function`, `ALTER SCHEMA` emits kind `namespace`, `ALTER EXTENSION` emits kind `import`, and the remaining object kinds (`TABLE`, `(MATERIALIZED) VIEW`, `SEQUENCE`, `SYNONYM`, `LOGIN`, `USER`, `ROLE`, `DATABASE`, `CERTIFICATE`, `INDEX`, `TYPE`, `DOMAIN`, `PARTITION SCHEME`, `FULLTEXT CATALOG`) emit kind `class`. Splitting the `ALTER` row by kind keeps the same object's `CREATE` and `ALTER` symbols under the same `kind` so `symbols --kind function` / `definition` / `inspect` do not duplicate across kinds. The `ALTER` side also now picks up `CERTIFICATE`, `DOMAIN`, and `EXTENSION` that were missing from the original row so every non-`TABLE` `ALTER` form is actually captured rather than just claimed. Every SQL row now shares an identifier shape that accepts PG double-quoted (`"name"`), T-SQL bracketed (`[name]`), or bare (`\w+`) tokens with optional dotted qualifiers such as `[dbo].[sp_X]`, `"schema"."name"`, and `schema.name`. The existing `CREATE INDEX ON tbl` / anonymous-name guard (`(?!ON\b)`), the `CREATE TYPE ... AS ENUM` Postgres branch, and the `CREATE SCHEMA AUTHORIZATION` branch are preserved. Body-less `namespace`-kind symbols from SQL (`CREATE SCHEMA sales;`, `ALTER SCHEMA sales TRANSFER ...;`) would previously trip the `IsFileScopedNamespace` check that wraps every subsequent top-level symbol under a C# `namespace X;` file-scoped declaration — so `ALTER FUNCTION dbo.fn_Total`, `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION pf_OrdersByYear`, and every later declaration in the same file were emitted with `container_kind='namespace'` / `container_name='sales'`, breaking `definition` / `inspect` / family grouping on real migration scripts. The helper now additionally requires the signature to start with the `namespace` keyword, so SQL schema rows no longer act as file-scoped containers; SQL schema scoping is still expressed through qualified names (`sales.Money`), matching how the rest of cdidx reads SQL. Added a dedicated `Extract_SQL_DetectsTSqlDdlKinds` regression test that locks all thirteen new T-SQL `CREATE` shapes and every new `ALTER` kind contract (`ALTER PROCEDURE` / `ALTER FUNCTION` / `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION` → `function`; `ALTER SCHEMA` → `namespace`; `ALTER EXTENSION` → `import`; `ALTER CERTIFICATE` / `ALTER DOMAIN` → `class`) including the `CREATE PROC` + `ALTER PROCEDURE` pair that must emit two `dbo.sp_DailyReport` rows both under kind `function`, and asserts that no later top-level SQL symbol is wrapped under `namespace=sales` so the file-scoped-namespace container pollution cannot regress. `GO` batch boundary awareness and `BEGIN ... END` structural nesting are deliberately out of scope here and remain filed in #230 as stretch items. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #230.

#### Fixed
- **SQL `CREATE` / `ALTER PROCEDURE` / `PROC` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` bodies now carry body ranges, so calls inside the body attribute to the enclosing proc (#429)** — `SymbolExtractor` emitted every `CREATE` / `ALTER PROCEDURE` / `PROC` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` with `BodyStyle.None`, leaving `BodyStartLine` / `BodyEndLine` null. `ReferenceExtractor.ResolveContainerForCall` → `FindInnermostContainer` relies on those ranges to attribute an in-body call to the enclosing procedure, so every call inside a procedure body fell through to the file-level fallback and `symbol_references.container_kind` / `container_name` were written as null. As a result `cdidx callers` / `callees` / `impact` returned zero for every SQL procedure even though `graph_supported` reported true. The procedure/function/trigger rows now emit a new `BodyStyle.SqlProcBody`, and the new `FindSqlProcBodyRange(lines, startIndex)` helper scans forward for (1) a balanced PostgreSQL dollar-quoted body (`$$ ... $$` / `$tag$ ... $tag$`) when the next non-blank payload begins with a dollar tag, (2) a T-SQL `GO` batch separator at line start (trailing `;` / `--` comment tolerated), (3) a new top-level DDL start (`CREATE` / `ALTER` / `DROP` / `GRANT` / `REVOKE` / `DENY` / `USE`), or (4) end-of-file. Before scanning each line, `MaskSqlLineForBodyScan` strips `--` line comments, `/* ... */` block comments, and `'..'` / `".."` string literals (preserving column width so later column alignment stays correct, and preserving `[name]` / `` `name` `` quoted identifiers because SQL quoted identifiers are not string literals) so a `GO` / `$$` / `CREATE` token embedded in a string or comment does not close the body early. `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION` is intentionally split into its own pattern and keeps `BodyStyle.None` because it modifies a partition boundary value rather than executable code, so its surface should remain body-less. Added eight `SymbolExtractor` regression tests covering T-SQL `BEGIN ... END` bodies terminated by `GO`, Postgres dollar-quoted function bodies, single-line `AS BEGIN ... END;` bodies, DDL-start close without an intervening `GO`, string/comment masking (a `GO` / `$$` / new `CREATE` inside a string literal or `--` comment does not close the body), `ALTER PROCEDURE` body capture, `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION` staying body-less, and a regression guard that a second procedure is not swallowed into the previous procedure's body range. Added two `ReferenceExtractor` regression tests: `Extract_SqlCallInsideProcedureBody_AttributesCallerToEnclosingProcedure` pins that an `EXEC` inside a T-SQL `CREATE PROCEDURE dbo.sp_Outer` body resolves to `ContainerKind=function` / `ContainerName=sp_Outer` while a post-`GO` call has null container, and `Extract_SqlPostgresDollarQuotedBody_AttributesCallerToEnclosingFunction` pins the same for a `PERFORM public.fn_inner()` inside a Postgres `$$ ... $$`-quoted `fn_outer` body. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #429.
- **Regression lock for C# interpolated and verbatim string reference extraction (#264)** — The original issue report alleged that `ReferenceExtractor` hid call-site references inside C# `$"..."` interpolation holes and leaked phantom references from `@"..."` verbatim string bodies. On the current `StructuralLineMasker` implementation the C# paths already handle single-line `$"..."`, multi-line `$@"..."` / `@$"..."`, and non-interpolated `@"..."` correctly — interpolation-hole call sites are captured with correct `ContainerName`, and multi-line verbatim bodies never leak phantom edges — but no regression test pinned that behavior end-to-end for the exact fixture in the issue report, so any future refactor of the masker's C# frame-stack handling could silently reintroduce the bug. Added `Extract_CsharpInterpolatedAndVerbatimStrings_Issue264_Repro_CapturesHoleCallsAndSuppressesPhantoms` which feeds the issue's exact fixture (`$"Hello {Helper.GetName()}"`, `$"Age: {Helper.GetAge()} years"`, `$"Nested {Helper.Format(Helper.GetName())}"`, a multi-line `$@"..."` with an interpolation hole, a plain non-interpolated call site, and a multi-line `@"..."` verbatim body containing `PhantomCall()` / `PhantomTable()` / `MoreFake()`) through `ReferenceExtractor.Extract` and pins four invariants at once: `Helper.GetName` is captured exactly four times, `Helper.GetAge` and `Helper.Format` are each captured at least once, every captured call's `ContainerName` resolves to `Work`, and no reference row ever surfaces for the phantom identifiers embedded in the verbatim body. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #264.
- **C# nested `new interface` (member-hiding a base-class nested interface) is now pinned by a dedicated regression (#376)** — Issue #376 reported that `public new interface INested { ... }` nested inside a derived class was silently dropped because the C# interface regex modifier list was `(?:partial|unsafe)` and did not include `new`. The free-modifier-order rewrite for #355 already widened the list to `(?:partial|unsafe|file|new)`, so the current binary already emits two `interface INested` symbols — one nested in `Base`, one nested in `Derived` — and the #376 repro is no longer reproducible. This change locks that behavior in with a dedicated `Extract_CSharp_NewNestedInterface_MemberHiding` regression that runs the exact fixture from the issue and asserts both nested interfaces are extracted (`ContainerName == "Base"` and `ContainerName == "Derived"`), so a future modifier-list edit cannot regress the #376 case without a failing test. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #376.
- **C# 8 `readonly` instance indexers on structs are now captured as `Item` symbols (#352)** — `SymbolExtractor` previously dropped `public readonly int this[int i] => _arr[i];` and `public readonly string this[string key] { get => key; }` silently, so `definition`, `symbols`, `outline`, and `inspect` undercounted `readonly`-heavy slice / span / immutable-wrapper struct surfaces. The indexer row already accepts `readonly` in the free-order modifier slot alongside `unsafe` / `extern` / `ref (readonly)` following the #355 rewrite, and this change locks that behavior in with a dedicated `Extract_CSharp_DetectsReadonlyIndexers` regression covering expression-body, block-body, and generic-return (`public readonly T this[int i] { get => _items[i]; }`) shapes plus non-readonly / readonly-method baselines so a future regex refactor cannot regress the #352 case without a failing test. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`.
- **`cdidx search` now caps per-line snippet width, so a single match in a minified / transpiled file no longer returns hundreds of KB of output (#196)** — `cdidx search --snippet-lines N` already limited the *number* of snippet lines returned per result, but it did not cap the *width* of each individual line. A match inside a minified / transpiled single-line file (one ~120 KB physical line), a generated fixture, or an obfuscated payload therefore returned the entire raw line verbatim — JSON output ballooned to hundreds of KB per result, human TUI output wrapped unreadably, the MCP `search` tool's `structuredContent` blew up AI token budgets, and the issue's repro (a 120,009-char Python line with one match) returned the full 120 KB payload even with `--snippet-lines 1`. `SearchSnippetFormatter` now runs every snippet line through the shared `LineWidthFormatter.ClampLine` helper already used by `find` / `references` / `excerpt` / `inspect`, so match lines are clamped around the first match token (keeping the token visible with surrounding `...(+N)...` markers) and non-match context lines head-clamp with a trailing `...(+N)...` marker. `SearchHighlight` now carries `OriginalLineLength` and `Truncated` fields so AI clients can detect clamped lines, and `CompactSearchResult` / `SearchSnippetExcerpt` expose a `TruncatedLineCount` summary field. The new `--max-line-width <n>` flag (CLI) and `maxLineWidth` argument (MCP `search`) share the exact same contract and defaults as the other commands (`DefaultMaxLineWidth=512`, `MaxAllowedLineWidth=4096`), so users and AI clients don't have to remember a separate knob for `search`. `--max-line-width` is added to the search usage line, help description, and bash / zsh / fish completions (fish already emitted `search` as a subcommand but previously did not advertise `--max-line-width` for it). The bash and zsh `search` completion branches are also realigned with the actual `RunSearch` contract — `--exact-name` (which `RunSearch` rejects with a usage error) is dropped from the candidate set, and the accepted `--top` (a `--limit` alias) and `--no-dedup` flags are added. The MCP `maxLineWidth` helper now also fails closed on values above `MaxAllowedLineWidth` (schema ceiling `4096`) instead of silently clamping them, so a schema-violating `maxLineWidth: 4097` now surfaces as an explicit tool error rather than a silently rewritten success. The CLI `--max-line-width` parser matches the same contract on `search` / `references` / `inspect` / `excerpt` (via `ParseArgs`) and `find` (via `ValidateFindArgs`): values above `MaxAllowedLineWidth` now abort with `UsageError` and empty stdout instead of silently falling back to `ClampMaxLineWidth`, so CLI and MCP agree on the ceiling contract that automation depends on. For `find` in particular, `ValidateFindArgs` is now inline-`=` aware — it uses `TrySplitInlineOptionValue` to read an inline `--opt=value` token as `(--opt, value)` for its own validation without rewriting the arg list, so the pre-flight validator no longer rejects the documented `--opt=<value>` form with `unsupported option for find: --max-line-width=4097` while the other query commands accept it through `ParseArgs`. The arg list passed on to `ParseArgs` is left untouched, so legitimate inline values that themselves start with `--` (e.g. `--path=--literal.txt` for a path literally named `--literal.txt`, exactly the shape the existing CLI hint recommends) are preserved verbatim for `ParseArgs` to handle. Smoke-tested against the issue's repro: a 120,009-char single-line file with one match now produces ~293 bytes of output by default, ~137 bytes at `--max-line-width 200`, and ~2085 bytes at `--max-line-width 4096`; the JSON `snippet` field carries the `...(+119914)...` marker around the first match token, and `truncated_line_count` / `highlights[].truncated` / `highlights[].original_line_length` are populated. Short lines that fit within `maxLineWidth` are unchanged. Added `SearchSnippetFormatter` regression tests pinning the long-match-line clamp, long non-match-line clamp, `CompactSearchResult` truncation metadata, and the "short line stays verbatim" guarantee, updated the `ConsoleUi` usage and help-text assertions, and added a `QueryEntrypoints_MaxLineWidthAboveCeilingFailClosed_Issue196` theory that drives `RunSearch` / `RunReferences` / `RunInspect` / `RunFind` / `RunExcerpt` with `--max-line-width 4097` (and `search` with `8192`) and pins the `UsageError` exit, empty stdout, the explicit `"--max-line-width must be less than or equal to 4096"` stderr message, and the `Usage:` line, with matching inline-`=` rows (`--max-line-width=4097`) for `search` / `references` / `inspect` / `find` / `excerpt` so the inline-`=` validator contract is pinned alongside the space-separated form, plus a `RunFind_PathFilterAcceptsRecognizedOptionTokenViaInlineValue` regression that drives `find Alpha --db=<db> --path=--json-dir --count --json` end to end and pins that `find` honors inline `--path=<value>` values starting with `--`, matching the `search` / `files` contract. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/SearchSnippetFormatter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SearchSnippetFormatterTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`. Closes #196.
- **Common language-specific filenames and extensions are no longer silently dropped from the index (#189)** — `FileIndexer.TryDetectLanguage` previously only mapped a handful of extensions and exact filenames, so everyday files that real projects ship — Ruby's `Gemfile` / `Rakefile` / `Podfile` / `Guardfile` / `Capfile` / `.rake` / `.gemspec` / `.podspec`, Podman's `Containerfile`, explicit `GNUmakefile`, Makefile variants `Makefile.common` / `Dockerfile.dev`, Bazel `BUILD` / `BUILD.bazel` / `WORKSPACE` / `WORKSPACE.bazel` (indexed as Python because Starlark is a Python dialect), Python stubs and Windows launcher scripts `.pyi` / `.pyw` (mapped to `python`), Cython `.pyx` / `.pxd` (mapped to their own `cython` bucket — search-only, because `cdef class` / `cpdef` / `cdef` are not parsed by the Python symbol extractor and advertising them as `python` would claim `symbol_extraction=true` while emitting zero symbols, the same mismatch that sunk the earlier `.sass` / `.styl` → `css` mapping), T-SQL / PostgreSQL / Oracle PL/SQL dialects `.tsql` / `.pgsql` / `.plsql` / `.psql`, `.htm`, CSS-family preprocessors `.less` / `.pcss` (mapped to `css`), indentation-based Sass `.sass` and Stylus `.styl` (mapped to their own `sass` / `stylus` buckets because the CSS symbol extractor is brace-based and cannot parse indented syntax — they are search-only, matching the current `cdidx languages` `symbol_extraction` contract), and plain `.mk` — were all treated as binary/unknown and skipped without a shebang fallback match. `LangMap` has been extended with the missing extensions, `FileNameMap` with the missing exact-match filenames, and a new `FileNamePrefixMap` handles the `Dockerfile.<suffix>` / `Containerfile.<suffix>` / `Makefile.<suffix>` / `GNUmakefile.<suffix>` pattern that is idiomatic on real Dockerfile and GNU Make projects. The prefix match requires a non-empty suffix (`fileName.Length > prefix.Length`) so bare trailing-dot inputs like `Dockerfile.` remain unrecognized rather than being misclassified, and the prefix check runs after the exact-filename check so existing `Dockerfile` / `Makefile` / `GNUmakefile` rows keep their original language mapping. Extension lookup still runs first so tool-specific extensions like `.gemspec` are not shadowed by an accidental `.rb`-style prefix collision. `GetLanguageExtensions()` — the public API behind `cdidx languages` and the MCP language listing — now also surfaces the prefix variants as `<Prefix><suffix>` pseudo-entries (`Dockerfile.<suffix>`, `Containerfile.<suffix>`, `Makefile.<suffix>`, `GNUmakefile.<suffix>`) so the advertised language list matches what `TryDetectLanguage` actually recognizes at scan time. Added `FileIndexer` regression coverage that pins every new extension, every new exact filename, every prefix variant, an end-to-end `ScanFiles` test that constructs all 10 files from the issue's repro and asserts exactly 10 files come back indexed (previously only 1 survived), a negative theory that locks `Dockerfile.` / `Containerfile.` / `Makefile.` / `GNUmakefile.` bare trailing-dot inputs out of the prefix map, and a dedicated `GetLanguageExtensions_ExposesPrefixAndFileNameVariants` test that pins the exact-name and prefix-variant entries plus the `sass` / `stylus` split away from `css`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #189.
- **`cdidx languages` human-readable table no longer lets long extension lists swallow the `Symbols` / `Graph` columns** — `QueryCommandRunner.RunLanguages` formatted each row with a fixed-width `{exts,-36}` column, so languages whose extension list was wider than 36 characters (`python` with Bazel `BUILD` files, `ruby` with `Gemfile` / `Rakefile` / `Vagrantfile`, `xml` with the MSBuild `.csproj` / `.props` / `.targets` family, and — after the #189 follow-up — `dockerfile` and `makefile` with their `<Prefix><suffix>` pseudo-entries) pushed the `Symbols` and `Graph` cells to the right of the Extensions string, where they visually merged with the extension list and became unreadable on narrow terminals. The latent regression was invisible in test coverage because `RunLanguages_JsonListsModernNodeModuleExtensions` only exercised the `--json` path. Long rows now spill the extension list onto a `  Extensions: ...` continuation line while short rows keep the existing single-line table, and a new regression test `RunLanguages_HumanOutput_WideExtensionListSpillsOntoContinuationLine` pins the behavior for every currently-wide language (including the `Dockerfile.<suffix>` / `Containerfile.<suffix>` / `Makefile.<suffix>` / `GNUmakefile.<suffix>` pseudo-entries) so future additions do not silently reintroduce the layout break. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`.
- **C#/Java `nameof(X.Y)` / `typeof(T)` / `default(T)` / `T.class` arguments are indexed as `type_reference` edges (#253)** — The shared `CallRegex` in `ReferenceExtractor` requires a trailing `(` to emit a call edge, so the arguments of C# `nameof(Target.Alpha)`, `typeof(Target)`, `sizeof(Target)`, `default(Target)`, and Java `Target.class` never matched and silently disappeared from `references`, `inspect`, and `impact`. The C# path now uses a regex only to locate the `nameof` / `typeof` / `sizeof` / `default` keyword and its opening `(`, then walks the argument body with a small lexer that skips generic `<...>` / array `[...]` / tuple `(...)` groups and `global::` / `Alias::` namespace-alias qualifiers so nested paths like `nameof(List<int>.Count)`, `nameof(System.Collections.Generic.Dictionary<string, int>.KeyCollection)`, and `nameof(global::System.String)` are captured end-to-end instead of truncating at the first `<` or stopping at the `Alias` token. The Java path keeps a regex-based match against `<ident>(.ident)*\s*(\[\s*\])*\.class` and splits dotted arguments. Each segment is emitted with `reference_kind='type_reference'` so call-graph tools that only care about invocations are not polluted. Each row carries the original column and context line, Java primitive segments (`int`, `long`, `short`, `boolean`, `byte`, `char`, `float`, `double`, `void`) and C# predefined-type alias segments (`bool`, `byte`, `sbyte`, `short`, `ushort`, `int`, `uint`, `long`, `ulong`, `nint`, `nuint`, `char`, `float`, `double`, `decimal`, `string`, `object`, `void`, `dynamic`, `var`) are filtered out because they resolve to BCL primitives rather than indexed user-defined symbols, and the shared ignore-call set is also applied. C# bare `default;` (no `(`) is intentionally not captured. On the read side, `DbReader.GetCallers` / `CountCallers` / `CountCallersTotal` / `GetCallees` / `CountCallees` / `CountCalleesTotal` now exclude `reference_kind='type_reference'` rows whenever `referenceKind == null`, so `callers`, `callees`, and `impact` do not regress on the new edges; `subscribe` edges continue to surface in default caller/callee output to preserve existing event-subscription semantics (pinned by existing `DbReaderTests`). `references` and `--kind type_reference` still surface the new edges. Added regression coverage for C# `nameof` / `typeof` / `default` argument segments (including multi-level dotted arguments, generic stripping mid-path, nested generics, `global::` / alias qualifiers, C# built-in-alias skipping, tuple element capture across inner parens such as `typeof((Foo, Bar))` / `default((Foo, Bar))` / `typeof((Foo, Bar)[])`, and bare-`default` negative), the column alignment of each segment against the original source line, and Java `T.class` / `outer.inner.class` / primitive skipping, bracket skipping, and the full chain. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #253.
- **`--since` thresholds with a time-of-day component silently returned zero results (#203)** — `cdidx files --since 2025-06-20T21:00:00Z`, `cdidx symbols --since ...`, `cdidx search ... --since ...`, `cdidx definition --count --since ...`, and every other command layered on the `ListFiles` / `CountListFiles` / `SearchSymbols` / `CountSearchSymbols` / `CountSearchSymbolsTotal` / `CountDefinitionsTotal` / `Search` / `CountSearchResults` / `ScopeMayIncludeCSharpFiles` read paths returned zero rows whenever the threshold carried a non-midnight time-of-day, even when matching files with later `modified` timestamps existed in the index. All nine of those read paths bound the `@since` SQL parameter via `since.Value.ToString("O")`, producing the ISO-8601 round-trip format `yyyy-MM-ddTHH:mm:ss.fffffffZ` with a `T` separator and trailing `Z`. `files.modified` is written by `DbWriter` with a DateTime parameter, which Microsoft.Data.Sqlite stores as TEXT in its default `DateTimeSqliteDefaultFormat` — `yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm:ss.FFFFFFF` with a space separator and no `Z`. SQLite compares TEXT values lexicographically, and because `T` (0x54) is greater than ` ` (0x20) at position 10, `f.modified >= @since` was always false. All nine `@since` bindings now pass `since.Value` directly so the read path serializes through the same Microsoft.Data.Sqlite DateTime formatter used by the write path, which keeps the format symmetric regardless of future Microsoft.Data.Sqlite format changes. Added eight `DbReaderTests` regression tests covering every count route that the issue-era code path silently broke — `ListFiles_WithTimeOfDaySince_IncludesNewerFiles`, `CountListFiles_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerFiles`, `SearchSymbols_WithTimeOfDaySince_IncludesNewerFiles`, `Search_WithTimeOfDaySince_IncludesNewerFiles`, `ListFiles_WithTimeOfDaySince_ExcludesFilesBeforeThreshold`, `CountSearchResults_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerChunks`, `CountSearchSymbolsTotal_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerSymbols`, `CountDefinitionsTotal_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerDefinitions` — that insert files whose `modified` timestamp straddles a 21:00 UTC threshold and pin that `--since` correctly includes later files and excludes earlier ones on every fixed code path, with bilingual comments documenting the root cause so the invariant can't silently regress to the old `ToString("O")` path. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSearchReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`. Closes #203.
- **`--lang` and `--kind` are now case-insensitive, and `WriteLangHint` now fires for `symbols` and `definition` (#199)** — `QueryCommandRunner.ParseArgs` previously stored `--lang` and `--kind` values verbatim, so `--lang Python` or `--kind FUNCTION` bypassed the SQL filters (every `files.lang` and `symbols.kind` row is lowercase) and returned 0 results. The same zero-result path on `symbols` and `definition` also skipped `WriteLangHint`, so users only saw the generic `try removing --lang, --path, ...` hint instead of the `'Python' not found in index. Available: python` hint that `search`, `references`, `callers`, `callees`, `inspect`, and `impact` already emit. `ParseArgs` now lowercases `--lang` / `--kind` at the parse site so every downstream SQL filter and hint comparison sees the normalized form, and `RunDefinition` / `RunSymbols` now call `WriteLangHint(options.Lang, reader)` alongside `WriteKindHint`, matching the other command surfaces. MCP `args["lang"]` / `args["kind"]` readers in `McpToolHandlers` apply the same lowercase normalization so MCP clients benefit from the same behavior. Added six regression tests in `QueryCommandRunnerTests`: `ParseArgs_NormalizesLangAndKindToLowercase` pins the parse-site normalization, `RunSymbols_AcceptsLangPythonCaseInsensitively` / `RunSymbols_AcceptsKindFunctionCaseInsensitively` / `RunDefinition_AcceptsLangPythonCaseInsensitively` pin that mixed-case values produce the same successful output as lowercase, and `RunSymbols_EmitsLangHintForUnknownLang` / `RunDefinition_EmitsLangHintForUnknownLang` pin the `Available: python` hint for unknown values. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #199.
- **`FileIndexer` no longer follows directory or file symlinks, preventing infinite recursion on ancestor loops and duplicate indexing (#190)** — `FileIndexer.EnumerateDirectory` previously enumerated subdirectories with a plain `Directory.EnumerateDirectories(dir)` and recursed unconditionally, with no reparse-point check and no visited-path tracking. A directory symlink pointing at an ancestor (e.g. `sub/parent_loop -> ..`) caused the indexer to walk `sub/parent_loop/sub/parent_loop/...` dozens of times until the OS path limit finally aborted recursion, indexing the same physical file under each synthetic path and polluting `symbols`, `files`, `outline`, `map` entrypoints while inflating index size. A milder symptom also affected file symlinks pointing at in-project files: the same content was indexed twice under two different paths. Both paths now check `FileAttributes.ReparsePoint` via a shared `IsReparsePoint` helper and skip symlinks without descending or reading. Directory symlinks are still recorded in `ListedDirectories` / `FullyScannedDirectories` so stale entries previously indexed under their synthetic paths get purged on the next full scan. Dangling symlinks (target missing) throw `FileNotFoundException` / `DirectoryNotFoundException` from `File.GetAttributes` and are treated as reparse points so the scan does not abort. The project root itself is unaffected — when the user explicitly points `cdidx index` at a symlinked directory, `_projectRoot` is used as the enumeration base, so the symlink is followed transparently by the OS. The reparse-point check also runs inside `GetFileIndexability`, so update paths (`cdidx index --files` / `--commits`), dry-run mode, and the Windows path all reject symlinks uniformly — `stat()`-based Unix probing would otherwise follow file symlinks silently and re-index the target under the link path. A new `SymlinkPrunedDirectories` set is threaded from `ScanFilesDetailed` through `ScanFilesResult` to `DbWriter.PurgeFilesOutsideRetainedSetWithinListedDirectories`, which now also purges deep descendants previously indexed under synthetic symlink ancestors (e.g. `sub/parent_loop/nested/a/b/c.py`) using a directory-boundary-safe `LastIndexOf('/')` ancestor walk, so re-indexing after an old loop-produced DB cleans up stale rows in one pass without collapsing sibling directories that happen to share a name prefix (`sub/parent_loop` vs `sub/parent_loop_sibling`). Added six regression tests: directory symlink to ancestor indexes once (not 40+ times), file symlink to in-project real file is deduplicated to a single row, a project containing only dangling file/directory symlinks still indexes the real files without aborting, `GetFileIndexability` rejects a file symlink so update-mode call paths skip it, deep descendants previously indexed under a symlink-pruned directory are purged on re-index, and the ancestor-walk prune does not confuse `sub/parent_loop` with sibling `sub/parent_loop_sibling/...`. Tests that create symlinks skip on Windows because creating symlinks there requires admin/developer mode. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DatabaseTests.cs`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #190.
- **C# declarations with non-canonical modifier order are no longer misclassified or dropped from symbol extraction (#355)** — C# grammar lets members and type declarations carry modifiers in any order (`public static readonly` ≡ `readonly public static` ≡ `static public readonly`, `public abstract class` ≡ `abstract public class`), but `SymbolExtractor` previously hard-coded visibility-first ordering on every C# row, so `readonly public static int E = 6;` fell through to the plain-field row and was emitted as kind `property` instead of kind `function` (losing the static readonly / const promotion), `static public int F() => 0;` lost its `visibility=public` (captured as empty), `abstract public class X {}` / `sealed public class Y {}` / `readonly public struct Z {}` / `ref public struct W {}` / `partial public interface I {}` were dropped entirely from `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` / `inspect`, `new public const int HiddenConst = 2;` (a compiler-legal same-name base-const hiding) was dropped from symbol extraction, and forms like `static public event System.EventHandler E1;` / `static public delegate int D1(int x);` / `static public int P1 { get; set; }` / `static public int this[int i] => 0;` / `static public explicit operator Money(...)` / `static public int operator +(...)` could drop or misclassify entirely. The affected rows — const field, static readonly field, conversion operator, operator overload, method (and its `delegate` negative-lookahead guard), brace-body property, expression-body property, delegate, event, indexer, interface, struct, class (including `record class` / `record`), and enum — now use a modifier alternation that accepts visibility at any position in the modifier sequence, and the static readonly field row uses two zero-width lookahead assertions (`(?=(?:...)*static\s+)` and `(?=(?:...)*readonly\s+)`) to enforce both keywords regardless of order (including `readonly new static`, `new readonly static`, and `static readonly new` interleaving). The method-row `delegate` negative lookahead is also widened to consume the same free-order modifier sequence, so real `public delegate int D(int x);` declarations continue to route to the dedicated delegate row and not get re-classified as methods. The plain-field (kind `property`) row is unaffected and still handles instance / readonly / volatile / plain static fields. Added five `SymbolExtractor` regression tests: `Extract_CSharp_StaticReadonlyField_FreeModifierOrder` pins seven orderings of the `static readonly` fixture (`public static readonly`, `public readonly static`, `public new static readonly`, `public readonly new static`, `public new readonly static`, `readonly public static`, `static readonly new`) as kind `function` and asserts none appear as kind `property`; `Extract_CSharp_Method_FreeModifierOrder` pins `static public`, `static internal`, `async public`, `override public`, and `virtual public` with the correct captured visibility; `Extract_CSharp_Property_ModifierBeforeVisibility` pins `static public int P1 { get; set; }`, `static public int P2 => 0;`, `virtual public int P3 { get; set; }`, `override public int P4 => 0;`, `static public event System.EventHandler E1;`, `static public delegate int D1(int x);`, and `static public int this[int i] => 0;` (indexer normalized to `Item` via `NormalizeCSharpSymbolName`); `Extract_CSharp_TypeDeclarations_FreeModifierOrder` pins `abstract public class`, `sealed public class`, `readonly public struct`, `ref public struct`, `partial public interface`, and `abstract public record class`; `Extract_CSharp_ConstField_FreeModifierOrder` pins `new public const int HiddenConst = 2;` and `public new const int HiddenConst2 = 3;` as kind `function` with `visibility=public` and `return_type=int`. The brace-body property, expression-body property, event, and indexer rows now also accept `unsafe` / `extern` in their free-order modifier sequence, the constructor row now accepts an `unsafe` / `extern` prefix either before or after the visibility token (`unsafe public S(int* p) {}` and `extern public S(int x);` previously captured with empty `visibility` and a polluted `return_type` that absorbed the leading modifier, or were dropped entirely for event / constructor shapes), and the static-constructor row now accepts `unsafe` before or after `static` (`unsafe static S()` ≡ `static unsafe S()`), so every compiler-legal `unsafe` / `extern` placement is captured with correct `visibility` and without the leading modifier bleeding into `return_type`. Added a sixth `SymbolExtractor` regression test `Extract_CSharp_UnsafeExtern_FreeModifierOrder` that pins `unsafe public` property (brace and expression body), `unsafe public` / `extern public` event, `unsafe public` indexer (normalized to `Item`), `unsafe public` / `extern public` constructors, and an `unsafe static` static constructor. The plain-field row and the multi-line field-header prefix regex (`CSharpPropertyHeaderPrefixRegex`) were also visibility-first and the header prefix did not accept `const`, so `static public int X;`, `readonly public int Y;`, the multi-line `static public Dictionary<string, int>` + `    Map = new();` shape, and the multi-line const `new public const int` + `    C = 1;` shape either dropped `visibility` or were dropped entirely from `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` / `inspect` / `unused`. Both regexes now accept visibility anywhere in the modifier sequence, the header prefix accepts `const` alongside the other field-eligible modifiers for the multi-line const case, and the field-header merger in `BuildCSharpPropertyMatchLine` now runs for both `property` and `function` kinds so `const` / `static readonly` field patterns (kind `function`) can see the merged header line. Non-field `function` patterns (methods, constructors, operators, indexers) are unaffected because `CSharpPropertyHeaderPrefixRegex` requires the line to end before `(` or `{`. Added a seventh regression test `Extract_CSharp_PlainField_FreeModifierOrder` covering `static public int X;`, `readonly public int Y;`, `new public static int Z = 1;`, the multi-line generic field, and the multi-line const. The event row also previously rejected the inheritance modifiers that are legal on event declarations per the C# spec (`virtual` / `override` / `abstract` / `sealed`), and the interface and delegate rows did not accept the `file` file-scoped type modifier (or `new` for nested delegate hiding), so `abstract public event System.EventHandler E;`, `virtual public event System.EventHandler E;`, `sealed public override event System.EventHandler E;`, `file interface I {}`, and `file delegate int D(int x);` were dropped from symbol extraction. The plain-field negative lookahead was also too narrow: because `abstract` / `virtual` / `override` / `sealed` / `async` / `partial` / `file` / `ref` were not in the rejected-leading-token list, a declaration like `abstract public event System.EventHandler A;` was matching the plain-field row with `return_type` absorbing `"abstract public event System.EventHandler"` and `visibility` left empty. Added `virtual` / `override` / `abstract` / `sealed` / `new` to the event modifier alternation, added `file` / `new` to the interface and delegate alternations, and added `abstract` / `virtual` / `override` / `sealed` / `async` / `partial` / `file` / `ref` to the plain-field negative lookahead so non-field leading modifiers can no longer bleed into `return_type`. Added an eighth regression test `Extract_CSharp_InheritanceAndFile_FreeModifierOrder` pinning `file interface`, `file delegate`, and four inheritance-modifier event forms (`abstract public`, `virtual public`, `sealed public override`, `new public`) with `visibility="public"`. Updated the C# language-pattern row in `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md` to note that modifier order is now accepted in any position. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #355.
- **POSIX filenames containing `\` no longer become phantom `/` subdirectories in the index (#191)** — `FileIndexer.BuildRecordWithRawBytes` and several CLI helpers (`GitHelper.GetChangedFilesFromCommit`, `IndexCommandRunner` full-scan / `--commits` / `--files` path normalization and `.git/info/exclude` computation, `QueryCommandRunner.RunOutline`) unconditionally ran `Replace('\\', '/')` on relative paths regardless of the host OS. On Windows that is correct because `\` is the directory separator, but on POSIX `\` is a legal filename character (data-science notebooks with awkward names, generated / escaped paths, adversarial filenames) so a single-component file called `back\slash.py` was silently rewritten to `back/slash.py`. The file was then stored as if there were a `back/` directory containing `slash.py`, `excerpt 'back\slash.py'` and `outline back\slash.py` returned "No excerpt found" / null because the DB key was the mangled form, `files` / `map` / `outline` advertised a phantom `back/` subdirectory that does not exist on disk, and AI clients building mental maps from those outputs wasted tool calls exploring the imaginary directory. Added a single `FileIndexer.NormalizePathSeparators` helper that only runs the `\`→`/` conversion when `Path.DirectorySeparatorChar == '\\'` (i.e. on Windows), and replaced all nine storage and lookup sites so Windows indexes still normalize separators while POSIX indexes preserve `\` inside filenames verbatim. Internal pattern-matching helpers (`NormalizeIgnorePath` for gitignore rules, `NormalizeScopeKey` for ambiguous-project scope grouping) are intentionally left unchanged because they operate on gitignore-style patterns, not filesystem-literal paths. Added a POSIX-gated `BuildRecord_PreservesBackslashInPosixFilename` unit test that creates a `back\slash.py` file on disk and asserts `record.Path` is stored as `back\slash.py`, a `GetExcerptAndOutline_RoundTripPathContainingBackslash` DB-level regression that pins `excerpt` / `outline` lookups succeed against the literal path and fail against the mangled `back/slash.py` form, and cross-platform unit tests for `NormalizePathSeparators` itself covering both the Windows-separator and POSIX-no-op branches. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/GitHelper.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`. Closes #191.
- **Multi-line C# enum members, JS/TS bare methods, and C# record primary-ctor headers no longer leak `\r` into signatures on CRLF sources (#405)** — `SymbolExtractor.GetSourceSpanText` (used to build C# enum member signatures via `TryAddCSharpEnumMemberFromSpan`), `TryCaptureJavaScriptTypeScriptMethodHeader` (used to build `Signature` for JS/TS class-body methods whose header wraps across physical lines), and `CollectRecordDeclarationText` (used internally to parse C# record primary-constructor components) all concatenated `lines[...]` slices with a literal `'\n'` separator without stripping the trailing `'\r'` that `content.Split('\n')` leaves on CRLF-terminated input. As a result, Windows / `autocrlf=true` / Visual Studio-saved sources produced signatures carrying OS-dependent `"\r\n"` between physical lines, breaking cross-OS signature equality, snapshot tests, and any downstream consumer that compared signatures by string equality. This is the same class of bug that `#382` fixed for `BuildCSharpTypeHeaderSignature`. All three paths now use a shared `StripTrailingCr` / `GetLineLengthExcludingTrailingCr` helper to drop one trailing `'\r'` per line before appending, so inter-line separators stay `'\n'` regardless of source line endings. For the JS/TS path, both the source builder and the sanitized builder strip in lockstep so the column-to-source mapping in `TryMapJavaScriptTypeScriptHeaderColumnToSourceLocation` stays aligned. Added three regression tests that construct CRLF-terminated content for each extractor path (a multi-line C# enum member span, a wrapped JS class-body method, and a wrapped C# record primary constructor) so the fix is pinned for every path. Bare-CR (old-Mac) line endings remain out of scope because `content.Split('\n')` does not split them at all. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #405.
- **Wrapped C# class / struct / interface / enum headers now preserve their base list and `where` clauses in `symbols.signature` (#382)** — `SymbolExtractor` previously sliced `SymbolRecord.Signature` for C# type declarations from the single physical line the declaration regex matched, so headers whose base list or generic constraints wrapped onto following lines — e.g. `public sealed class Foo<T>\n    : BaseFoo<T>, IBar, IBaz\n    where T : class, new()\n{` — truncated to `public sealed class Foo<T>` and silently lost every `:` base, interface, and `where T : ...` clause. Downstream consumers that read the signature to recover the base type (the planned `ParseCSharpBaseType` path in #257, future type-position reference extraction for #256, any lint or `impact` / `analyze_symbol` flow that wants to answer "what does this class extend?" from the index alone) degraded to "no base type" for every wrapped-header C# class on every large library that uses formatter-wrapped headers (ASP.NET Core, Roslyn, EF Core, xUnit, `Microsoft.Extensions.*`, etc.). The C# signature path now extends the existing multi-line-signature mechanism (already used for properties) to type declarations: a new `TryFindCSharpTypeHeaderExtent` helper scans forward from the header start using `LexCSharpLine` so `{` / `;` inside string literals, comments, and verbatim / raw strings are ignored, tracks paren depth (C# 12 primary constructor parameter lists) and bracket depth (attributes on type or generic parameters) so a nested `{` / `;` can never short-circuit the scan, terminates at the first body-opening `{` or primary-constructor / forward-declaration `;` at zero depth, and caps lookahead at 64 lines to stay safe on unterminated input. A dedicated `BuildCSharpTypeHeaderSignature` assembles the header slice by concatenating the relevant `[startColumn, endColumn)` span from each physical line with a literal `'\n'` between lines, then runs the combined text through a single-pass `SanitizeCSharpTypeHeaderSlice` that strips `//` line comments (terminated at the next `'\n'`) and `/* ... */` block comments, collapses runs of Code-mode whitespace (including the newlines between lines) into a single space, and preserves String / Verbatim / Raw / Char literal contents verbatim — including multi-line raw / verbatim strings, which keep every internal line break and leading indentation instead of being `Trim()`ed and space-joined. The sanitizer also tracks C# interpolation holes with an explicit frame stack: `$"..."`, `$@"..."`, `@$"..."`, `$"""..."""`, and `$$"""{{expr}}"""` each push a String / Verbatim / Raw frame marked `Interpolated`, and a hole opens only when the `{` run is at least as long as the number of `$` prefixes (with `{{` and `}}` still honored as literal-brace escapes in non-raw interpolated strings). Inside a hole, the sanitizer re-enters Code mode and matching nested braces before returning to the outer literal, so `$"{@"a  b"}  c"` now keeps the inner verbatim literal's double-space intact and the outer literal content `  c` is preserved instead of the previous collapse to `a b` + ` c`. The helper still produces signatures like `public sealed class Foo<T> : BaseFoo<T>, IBar, IBaz where T : class, new()` for plain wrapped headers, and literal-bearing declarations like `record Foo(string S = "a  b")`, `@"C:\tmp\   spaces"`, `"""a   b"""`, multi-line raw-string primary-constructor defaults, and interpolation holes containing nested verbatim strings all keep every internal space and newline exactly as written. Same-line headers, single-line bodies, and the existing multi-line property path are unchanged. Added `SymbolExtractor` regression coverage for wrapped class + base list + `where` clauses, wrapped interface + multi-base + `where`, wrapped record primary constructor + wrapped base list + `where`, wrapped struct + `IEquatable<Value<T>>` + `where T : IComparable<T>`, wrapped enum + underlying type `: byte`, a same-line-class pin, dedicated wrapped-header + `//` line comment and wrapped-header + `/* ... */` block comment pins so comment-stripping cannot regress, wrapped primary-constructor-header pins for regular string, verbatim string, and raw string defaults so the lexer-aware collapse cannot silently rewrite literal whitespace, a multi-line raw-string default pin so newlines and per-line indentation inside multi-line raw strings cannot be destroyed by cross-line collapsing, and a nested-verbatim-inside-interpolation-hole pin so interpolation holes inside wrapped base-list arguments cannot exit the outer string too early and collapse inner literals. `BuildCSharpTypeHeaderSignature` also trims a trailing `'\r'` from every sliced line before appending the inter-line `'\n'`, so CRLF-terminated sources (Windows CI with `autocrlf=true`, files saved from Visual Studio, etc.) produce the same signature as LF-terminated sources instead of carrying OS-dependent `"\r\n"` separators between lines; a dedicated CRLF-content regression test pins that normalization. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #382.
- **Regression lock for out-of-range numeric query options (#161)** — `QueryCommandRunner` already rejects invalid `--limit` / `--depth` / `--before` / `--after` / `--start` / `--end` / `--snippet-lines` values with exit code 1, but the existing entrypoint coverage only exercised the non-parseable `"nope"` path. The original bug was specifically about valid integers (`0`, `-5`, `-1`) that parse successfully but fail the positive / non-negative constraint — those used to silently fall back to defaults and emit real results on stdout with exit 0, so callers that branch on exit code alone treated the default-backed output as authoritative. Added a dedicated regression theory `QueryEntrypoints_OutOfRangeNumericOptionsFailClosed_Issue161` that drives `RunSymbols`, `RunSearch`, `RunImpact`, and `RunExcerpt` with the exact repro values from the issue (`--limit 0` / `--limit -5`, `--snippet-lines 0`, `--depth -1`, `--start 0` / `--start -5`, `--end 0`, `--before -1`, `--after -1`) and pins three invariants at once: exit code is `UsageError`, stderr carries the expected `--<option> requires a ...` message with the offending raw value, and stdout is strictly empty so default-backed output cannot leak. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #161.
- **C# LINQ query-expression continuations no longer leak phantom method symbols (#377)** — The method regex and explicit-interface-implementation regex in `SymbolExtractor` now add the C# LINQ query-expression contextual keywords (`from`, `where`, `select`, `orderby`, `group`, `join`, `let`, `into`, `on`, `equals`, `ascending`, `descending`, `by`) to their statement-keyword negative lookaheads. Previously a continuation line like `where Validator.Check(x)` / `select Mapper.Convert(x)` / `orderby Math.Abs(x)` could satisfy the explicit-interface shape (`returnType=<linq-keyword>` + `qualifier.member(`) and emit phantom `function Check` / `function Convert` / `function Abs` rows alongside the real definitions, silently polluting `symbols`, `definition`, `callers`, `inspect`, and `hotspots` wherever qualified static helper calls appear inside LINQ query syntax. The lookahead is anchored to the line-leading token, so only bare continuation lines are rejected; regular method declarations whose name happens to be a LINQ keyword (such as `public void where() { }`) still match through their return type and are indexed as before. Added a `SymbolExtractor` regression test that locks the full LINQ query-expression repro (`where`, `select`, `orderby`, `group` / `by` / `into`, `join` / `on` / `equals`, `ascending`, `descending`, `let = ...`) with qualified static helper calls — every individual keyword appears in a line-leading position so each arm of the guard is exercised — and asserts that no phantom `function` rows surface for the helper member names and that real helper definitions still appear exactly once each. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #377.
- **C# explicit-interface property implementations now surface as `property` symbols, and multi-argument generic qualifiers are honored on both explicit-interface properties and methods (#333)** — `SymbolExtractor` now matches both brace-body (`int IThing.Value { get; set; }`) and expression-body (`string IThing.Name => "x";`) explicit-interface property implementations with dedicated C# rows that mirror the existing explicit-interface method row: the interface qualifier is non-capturing so the short property name (`Value`, `Name`) is recorded as the symbol name, consistent with how `Dispose` and `CompareTo` are exposed for explicit-interface methods. The shared `CSharpExplicitInterfaceQualifierPattern` has also been widened to accept the same shape that `CSharpTypePattern` uses for regular return types — comma-separated type arguments with internal spaces, nullable-typed arguments, and array-typed arguments — so qualifiers like `IMap<string, int>.PairCount`, `IFoo<string?>.Nullable`, and `IFoo<int[]>.ArrayArg` no longer silently drop. Because both the property rows and the pre-existing method row share the qualifier pattern, the same fix also repairs explicit-interface methods with multi-argument generic qualifiers (for example `int IMap<string, int>.GetCount() => 0;`), which the previous narrower qualifier pattern had quietly skipped. Generic interface qualifiers like `IBucket<int>.Items`, generic / alias-qualified return types, and `ref readonly` explicit-interface properties are all supported. The statement-keyword negative lookahead mirrors the regular property rows so `return o switch { ... }` style expressions cannot misclassify as properties. Without the fix those declarations were silently dropped from `symbols`, `definition`, `references`, `callers`, `callees`, `inspect`, and `outline`. Added extractor regression coverage for brace-body, expression-body, generic-interface, `ref readonly`, multi-argument generic, nullable-argument, and array-argument explicit-interface property implementations, and extended the existing explicit-interface method regression with multi-argument generic, nullable-argument, and array-argument method forms. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #333.
- **C# plain fields are now indexed as symbols (#298)** — `SymbolExtractor` previously only captured `const` and `static readonly` fields as C# symbols, so ordinary declarations like `public int Count;`, `private readonly List<int> _items;`, `protected volatile bool _ready;`, and `public static int GlobalCount;` were invisible to `definition`, `symbols`, `outline`, `inspect`, `hotspots`, and `unused`. Added a dedicated plain-field pattern that runs after the existing `const` / `static readonly` patterns and before the structural declaration patterns, captures the visibility and return type, and emits kind `property` (consistent with the taxonomy that already covers regular properties and record primary components). The terminator is `=(?![=>])` or `;`, which excludes methods (`(`), property accessors (`{`), expression-bodied members (`=>`), and comparison-operator overloads (`==`). The negative lookahead repeats every visibility and modifier keyword so the regex engine cannot backtrack past an unconsumed `public static event EventHandler OnClick;` declaration and misclassify it as a field whose returnType is `public static event EventHandler`. A scope tracker built from `StructuralLineMasker` output gates the new pattern to lines that sit directly inside a type body (`class` / `struct` / `interface` / `record` / `enum`), so local variable declarations inside method / property accessor / constructor / lambda bodies — which share the same shape as fields — are no longer misclassified as phantom `property` symbols and no longer leak into `symbols`, `definition`, `outline`, `inspect`, or `unused`. Field detection also extends beyond the single-line shape: the match line is now concatenated across multiple physical lines until the terminating `;` is reached (so `private Dictionary<string, int>` on one line followed by `    _map = new();` on the next is indexed as a single `_map` field with return type `Dictionary<string,int>`), the multi-line header prefix also accepts field-only modifiers such as `volatile`, `unsafe`, and `extern` so declarations like `private volatile Dictionary<string, int>\n    _map;` are no longer rejected at the header-prefix gate, the continuation walk tracks paren/bracket/brace depth until a top-level `;` is reached so parenthesized initializers such as `private Lazy<int>\n    _value = new(\n        () => 42);` merge all the way through the `(` instead of short-circuiting at the first parenthesis, multi-line fields whose initializer opens its own object or collection initializer — such as `private Dictionary<string, int>\n    _map = new()\n    {\n        ["a"] = 1\n    };`, `private List<int>\n    _list = new() {\n        1, 2, 3\n    };`, and `private Dictionary<string, int>\n    _typed = new Dictionary<string, int>\n    {\n        ["b"] = 2\n    };` — now continue past the initializer braces until the real top-level `;` closes the declaration (the accessor check still claims genuine property bodies first, so `{` is only treated as initializer scope once it is known not to start a property block), brace detection against the combined match line now runs on the structurally sanitized line instead of the raw source so `{` appearing inside a string literal or comment (for example `private string\n    _open = "{";` and `private string\n    _pair = "{" + "}";`) no longer flips the multi-line field path into property-body handling and silently drops the declaration, declarator lists such as `private int _x, _y;`, `public string First, Second, Third;`, and `private int _a = 1, _b, _c = 3;` now emit one symbol per declarator (each with the shared return type and its own per-declarator initializer stripped) instead of one symbol whose `return_type` silently contains a trailing comma, the declarator-list tail scanner now distinguishes generic `<`/`>` from comparison operators via a token-aware lookahead so initializers like `private int _a = x < y ? 1 : 2, _b;` or `private int _e = new Dictionary<int, int>() { [x < y ? 1 : 2] = 0 }.Count, _f;` no longer inflate the angle depth indefinitely and drop the trailing declarators, and the `delegate\b` negative lookahead is relaxed to `delegate\b(?!\*)` so function-pointer fields like `public delegate*<int, void> Callback;` and `private delegate* unmanaged[Cdecl]<int, int> _op;` pass through the plain-field path while real `public delegate int Callback(int x);` type declarations still continue to be handled by the dedicated `delegate` pattern. Added regression coverage for instance, readonly, volatile, plain static, protected-with-initializer, internal-volatile, and generic `Dictionary<string, int>` field shapes, for multi-line field declarations that wrap before `;`, for multi-line fields that rely on `volatile` / `unsafe` modifiers and function-pointer return types, for multi-line fields whose initializer uses a constructor call or parenthesized expression (including bodies that contain a lambda), for multi-line fields whose initializer uses object / collection initializers with `new() { ... };`, `new() { ... };` on a same-line brace, and `new Dictionary<...> { ... };`, for multi-line fields whose initializer contains `{` inside a string literal, for declarator-list fields (including mixed-initializer shapes and an assertion that no emitted symbol ever has a comma-contaminated `return_type`), for declarator-list fields whose initializer uses comparison operators inside generic-shaped constructs, for `delegate*` and `delegate* unmanaged[Cdecl]` function-pointer fields, plus a negative test pinning that real named-`delegate` type declarations are not misclassified as fields, a dedicated negative test that locks ctor-locals, method-locals, nested-block-locals, accessor-locals, and lambda-body-locals out of the symbol index, and a CLI end-to-end `QueryCommandRunner.RunSymbols` test that round-trips the multi-line / declarator-list / function-pointer shapes through indexer, DB, and `symbols --exact`, updated the developer guide C# language-pattern row to call out the new field coverage, and updated the README query-strategy section (English and Japanese) so users and AI clients see `public int Count;`, `private readonly List<int> _items;`, `public delegate*<int, void> Callback;`, and `cdidx symbols --lang csharp --kind property --name Count --exact-name` as first-class examples. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `README.md`. Closes #298.
- **C# inline and standalone attributes with bracket-bearing string literals no longer mis-bucket adjacent symbols in `unused` (#375)** — `DbSymbolReader.StripLeadingCSharpAttributeLists` was called on raw source lines without sanitizing C# string literals, so an inline attribute whose argument string contained `[` or `]` (e.g. `[JsonPropertyName("a[")] public string X { get; set; }`) was mis-parsed as "no inline declaration" by `LineContainsInlineAttributeAndDeclaration`. `GetAdjacentAttributeBlock` then treated that line as a free-standing attribute block and leaked the attribute context to the next property line, causing an adjacent plain property to be incorrectly classified as `reflection_or_config_suspect` in `unused`. The same class of bug also surfaced on the standalone-attribute path: `GetAdjacentAttributeBlock`'s upward scan used `CountChar(line, ']') - CountChar(line, '[')` to track bracket depth, so a standalone attribute line like `[Obsolete("]")]` above an unrelated property left one phantom bracket of depth and swallowed the previous member's reflection attribute block upward. The indexer path in `SymbolExtractor` was not affected because it already feeds `LexCSharpLine`-sanitized input into its strip. The DB-reader strip is now string-literal aware via a new `TrySkipCSharpStringOrCharLiteral` helper covering regular `"..."`, verbatim `@"..."`, raw `"""..."""` (C# 11, including longer quote runs), interpolated `$"..."`, interpolated verbatim `$@"..."` / `@$"..."`, raw interpolated `$"""..."""` and multi-`$` variants like `$$"""..."""` (where N consecutive `$` require N consecutive `{` / `}` to open / close interpolation while fewer are literal), and char `'...'` literals, `GetAdjacentAttributeBlock`'s standalone upward scan now uses a new `CountBracketDeltaOutsideStrings` helper that reuses the same string-literal skipper instead of naive `CountChar`, and the function refuses to carry an attribute block across a line that already declares a member on the same line. Added regression coverage that pins both the inline "adjacent plain property is not suspect" and "inline reflection attribute with bracket-in-string is still suspect" shapes, including verbatim, raw, raw-interpolated, and multi-`$` raw-interpolated variants, plus a standalone-attribute regression where a `[Obsolete("]")]` on its own line above a plain property must not swallow a real reflection attribute above it. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`. Closes #375.
- **T-SQL `EXEC` / `EXECUTE` / `CALL` stored-procedure references without trailing parens are now captured (#232)** — `ReferenceExtractor` previously only matched SQL procedure calls through the shared `CallRegex`, which requires a trailing `(` after the identifier. Real-world T-SQL almost exclusively uses the no-parens form (`EXEC dbo.sp_Target @a=1, @b=2;`, `EXECUTE [dbo].[sp_Target];`, MySQL / MariaDB `CALL sp_Target;`, `EXEC @retval = dbo.sp_Target ...`), so stored-procedure calls silently disappeared from `references`, `inspect`, `callers`, and `impact` on SQL codebases, leaving cross-procedure chains invisible. A new compiled regex `SqlProcCallRegex` locates `EXEC` / `EXECUTE` / `CALL` at word boundaries, optionally skips T-SQL return-value assignment (`@retval =`), and captures the terminal identifier (including `[bracketed names]` and multi-part `[dbo].[proc]` forms), stripping any enclosing brackets and adjusting the emitted column so the reference points at the identifier's real position. The match is case-insensitive and runs against the sanitized line produced by `PrepareLine`, so `EXEC` inside a string literal or comment is still naturally ignored. Ambiguous keywords that follow `EXECUTE` in other dialects — `AS` (T-SQL `EXECUTE AS USER='...'`) and `IMMEDIATE` (Oracle `EXECUTE IMMEDIATE ...`) — are added to the SQL ignore list with case-insensitive comparison so they can no longer surface as phantom procedure calls. The SQL ignore list also rejects the keywords `EXEC` / `EXECUTE` / `CALL` themselves so that T-SQL dynamic-SQL forms such as `EXEC(@sql)`, `EXEC('SELECT 1')`, and `EXECUTE(@sql)` — where the argument is a string or variable, not an identifier — cannot trigger a phantom `call EXEC` / `call EXECUTE` / `call CALL` edge through the generic `CallRegex`. Bracketed T-SQL identifiers (used in real code specifically to quote reserved words as object names, e.g. `EXEC [ORDER]`, `CALL [USER]`, `EXEC [dbo].[IMMEDIATE]`) skip the keyword ignore list after bracket stripping, so legitimate brace-quoted proc names whose inner text happens to match a SQL keyword are no longer silently dropped. A dedup key of `{lineNumber}:{column}:{referenceKind}:{name}` ensures the parenthesized form (`EXEC dbo.sp_Target();` and its bracketed variant `EXEC [dbo].[sp_Target]()`) still emits a single edge when both `SqlProcCallRegex` and the generic `CallRegex` would fire at the same position — `SqlProcCallRegex`'s post-bracket-stripping column adjustment keeps the two regexes converging on the same dedup key. Added regression tests in `ReferenceExtractorTests.cs` covering: no-parens extraction across `EXEC` / `EXECUTE` / `CALL` with plain, qualified, bracketed, and multi-segment bracketed forms; linked-server four-part names `EXEC server.db.schema.proc`; return-value assignment form; `EXECUTE AS USER='dbo'` / `EXECUTE IMMEDIATE 'sql'` negative coverage; string-literal safety (`EXEC sp_InsideString` inside a literal does not emit, but the outer `EXEC sp_executesql @sql` does); dedup parity between the parenthesized and no-parens forms (both plain and bracketed); the MySQL `CALL proc(args)` form with arguments; Unicode bracketed identifiers (`[名前]`, `[Ñoño]`, `[Процедура]`); `EXEC(@sql)` / `EXEC('...')` / `EXECUTE(@sql)` / `CALL(@sql)` dynamic-SQL negative coverage that pins no phantom EXEC / EXECUTE / CALL keyword edges; bracketed reserved-word identifier coverage (`[ORDER]`, `[AS]`, `[IMMEDIATE]`, `[USER]`) that pins legitimate calls survive after bracket stripping; and a non-word bracketed identifier coverage (`[#tempProc]` for T-SQL temp procedures, `[proc-name]` for hyphenated names, `[proc.v2]` for dotted versioned names) that pins the bracket character class accepts any character except `[`, `]`, or a line terminator so temp-proc and hyphenated real-world identifiers are captured and the preceding qualifier `[dbo]` is not misattributed as the proc name; omitted-qualifier-segment coverage (`EXEC AdventureWorks..sp_GetCustomer;`, `EXEC [AdventureWorks]..[proc-name];`, `EXEC srv.db..sp_with_omitted_schema;`) that pins SQL Server's four-part naming with a skipped database or schema still terminates on the real procedure name rather than falling back to the first qualifier segment; MySQL / MariaDB backtick-quoted identifier coverage (`` CALL `proc-name`; ``, `` CALL db.`proc-name`; ``, `` CALL `mydb`.`do_stuff`; ``) that pins backtick quoting is preserved through line sanitization and the terminal identifier is the captured target without the qualifier surfacing as a phantom call; and a backtick-quoted reserved-word coverage (`` CALL `order`; ``, `` CALL `select`; ``) that pins the ignore-list bypass after quote stripping, mirroring the existing bracketed `[ORDER]` / `[AS]` behavior. The internal identifier character class in `SqlProcCallRegex` therefore accepts three forms — `\[[^\[\]\r\n]+\]`, `` `[^`\r\n]+` ``, or bare `\w+` — in both qualifier and terminal-name positions, and qualifier segments themselves are optional so consecutive dots (`..`) do not abort the match. A dedicated `SqlStringLiteralRegex` + `PrepareSqlLineForIdentifierScan` helper sanitizes SQL lines for the `EXEC` / `EXECUTE` / `CALL` scan: unlike the shared `PrepareLine` it keeps backtick content intact (because backticks are identifier quoting in SQL, not string literals) while still stripping `'...'` / `"..."` literals and `--` / `#` / `/* ... */` comments so text inside a comment does not emit a phantom reference. The `--` and `#` line-comment scans track backtick and bracket identifier quoting so a legitimate `` CALL `proc#1`; `` or `EXEC [proc-name]` is not truncated mid-identifier even when the inner text contains `#` or `-`. A regression test `Extract_SqlHashCommentedCall_DoesNotEmitReference` pins the MySQL `# ...` comment behavior and a `Extract_SqlCallBacktickIdentifierContainingHash_IsCaptured` pin keeps `` CALL `proc#1`; `` alive. Also mentions `MySQL / MariaDB` rather than `SQL-PSM` in documentation, since the current implementation intentionally does not treat ANSI / SQL-PSM `"..."` delimited identifiers as identifier quoting (they still run through the string stripper). Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #232.
- **C# / Java constructor chain calls `: this(...)` / `: base(...)` / `super(...)` now show up as references (#257)** — `ReferenceExtractor` now rewrites C# constructor initializer chains and the equivalent Java constructor-body statements into `call` references pointing at the real target: `: this(args)` / `this(args);` resolves to the enclosing class or record, while `: base(args)` / `super(args);` parses the base type from the enclosing class signature (stripping generics, record primary-ctor args, `where` constraints, `global::` / dotted namespace qualifiers, and ignoring trailing interface entries in the base list). Cross-line C# initializers are attributed to the owning constructor rather than the enclosing class, C# records with `Parent(Value)` primary-ctor chaining get a synthetic function-kind container named after the record so the base call is attributed to the record itself instead of no container at all — the synthetic container now spans the full record declaration header up to the first `;` or `{`, so continuation-line forms like `public record Child(int Value, int Extra)\n    : Parent(Value);` attribute the base call to the record instead of leaving it in no container. Base-type parsing on both languages now uses a depth-aware scanner that splits on `.` / `::` at generic depth 0 and returns the terminal segment, so nested types under generic outer types such as `Outer<int>.Base` (C#), `Outer<Integer>.Base` (Java), and `global::Ns.Outer<T>.Inner` now resolve to `Base` / `Inner` instead of being misattributed to `Outer` and silently mis-aimed in `callers` / `callees` / `impact`. C# `: base(...)` resolution now reconstructs the full enclosing type header from structural lines (reusing the record primary-ctor header helper) instead of trusting `SymbolRecord.Signature`, which only captures the first declaration line, so formatter-style multi-line base-lists such as `class Child\n    : Parent`, `class Child<T>\n    : Outer<T>.Base`, and `class Child<T>\n    : Parent<T>\n    where T : class, new()` no longer silently drop the chain edge. Java `super(...)` resolution mirrors the same reconstruction, so multi-line `extends` forms such as `class Leaf\n    extends Base { Leaf(){super(0);} }`, `class Leaf\n    extends Outer<Integer>.Base {...}`, and `sealed class Leaf\n    extends Base\n    permits None` no longer drop the chain edge either. Java 17+ sealed-type declarations are supported too: the Java base-type scanner now treats `permits` as a word-boundary terminator alongside `implements`, so `sealed class Leaf extends Base permits A, B { Leaf(){super(0);} }` and `extends Outer<Integer>.Base permits A` resolve to `Base` instead of greedily absorbing `permits` into the returned type. Java package-private constructors that SymbolExtractor records without body ranges are found by a name-based fallback against the enclosing class so `Leaf(int x){super(x);}` still attributes the chain edge to the `Leaf` constructor, Java same-line ctor bodies such as `Leaf(int x){super(x);}` / `Leaf(){this(0);}` (which SymbolExtractor skips because the line ends with `}` instead of `{`/`,`/`;`) are handled by relaxing the ctor-chain regex to also match after `{` and by synthesizing a ctor container directly from the declaration line. The declaration-line scanner is depth-aware so it accepts fully qualified annotations with optional nested-paren argument lists (e.g. `@demo.Ann Leaf(int x){super(x);}`, `@SuppressWarnings({"unused", "unchecked"}) Leaf(...)`) and nested generic bounds on ctor type parameters (e.g. `public <T extends Comparable<Integer>> Leaf(T x){super(0);}`, `<U extends java.util.List<? extends Number>> Leaf(...)`), so annotated and generic same-line ctors are no longer silently dropped as class-scope phantom edges, and Java `this(...)` is added to the Java ignore set so the generic call scanner does not emit a phantom `call this` edge after the chain is rewritten. Java `super.method()` is still left alone as a regular call. `callers`, `references`, `callees`, and `impact` now surface the missing chain edges so a rename of a base constructor no longer looks safe when every subclass constructor chains to it. Java base-type resolution also strips JLS 9.7.4 type-use annotations before extracting the terminal segment, so `class Leaf extends @Ann Root`, `extends @pkg.Ann(value=1) Root`, `extends @Ann @Other Root`, and `extends Outer<Integer>.@Ann Base` resolve to the real base type instead of a phantom `@Ann Root` / `@Ann Base` name that silently misattributes `super(...)` edges. The base-list scanner also tracks `(...)` depth alongside `<...>` depth so commas inside annotation arguments such as `@Ann(a = 1, b = 2) Root`, `@Ann({A.class, B.class}) Root`, and `@pkg.Ann(value = {1, 2, 3}) Root` are no longer mistaken for top-level base-list separators (which previously truncated the segment before the annotation stripper could run and dropped the `super(...)` edge entirely). Java enums can declare constructors and chain via `this(...)`, so the enclosing-type candidate list and the innermost-class-like lookup now include `enum` alongside `class` / `struct` / `interface`; `enum Shade { Red, Blue(1); Shade(){ this(0); } Shade(int code){} }` now emits the chain edge to the enum instead of being silently dropped (C# enum is a no-op here because it cannot declare constructors and the C# chain regex never matches inside one). Added regression coverage for C# `: this(...)` / `: base(...)` (including generic bases, records attributed to the synthetic constructor, multi-line record continuation-line base calls, braced record bodies after a base call, cross-line wraps, `global::` base types, nested types under generic outer types such as `Outer<int>.Base` and `global::Ns.Outer<T>.Inner`, plain multi-line class base-lists like `class Child\n    : Parent`, multi-line nested-generic base-lists like `class Child<T>\n    : Outer<T>.Base`, and multi-line base-lists followed by `where` constraints) and Java `super(...)` / `this(...)` (including package-private constructors, public and package-private same-line ctor bodies for both `super(...)` and `this(...)`, same-line ctor bodies with leading annotations, same-line ctor bodies with generic type parameters, fully qualified annotations with nested-paren argument lists, nested generic bounds on ctor type parameters, nested types under generic outer types such as `Outer<Integer>.Base`, sealed / non-sealed / `permits`-bearing declarations including `extends Outer<Integer>.Base permits A`, multi-line `extends` base-lists like `class Leaf\n    extends Base`, multi-line `extends Outer<Integer>.Base`, multi-line `extends` with continuation-line `permits`, JLS 9.7.4 type-use annotated `extends` (`extends @Ann Root`, `extends @pkg.Ann Root`, `extends @Ann(value=1) Root`, `extends @Ann @Other Root`, `extends Outer<Integer>.@Ann Base`, `extends @Ann Outer<Integer>.Base`, `extends @Ann Root implements Foo`) including the E2E `super(...)` paths that would have pointed at a phantom annotated type, Java enum `this(...)` constructor chain attribution, and phantom `this` suppression). Java same-line ctor name extraction now accepts `@annotation` and `public` / `protected` / `private` / `static` / `final` / `abstract` modifiers in any order so formatter-style forms like `public @Deprecated Leaf(int x){super(x);}` and `@demo.Ann private Leaf(){this(0);}` no longer silently drop the chain edge when an annotation sits between modifiers instead of before them. The multi-line header collector is also depth-aware in `()` / `[]` / `<>` depth so `{` / `;` inside annotation arguments, array initializers, or generic bounds (e.g. `extends @Ann({A.class, B.class}) Root {`) no longer truncate the enclosing-type header before the real base type; this helper feeds both Java multi-line `extends` resolution and C# record primary-ctor container synthesis. `SymbolExtractor.FindBraceRange` is now also depth-aware in `()` / `[]` so that `{` / `}` inside annotation-argument and attribute-argument braces (`@Ann({A.class, B.class})`, array-initializer arguments, annotation-nested `{}`) do not count as body braces and no longer collapse the enclosing type's body range to a single line. Without that fix, `class Leaf extends @Ann({A.class, B.class}) Root { Leaf() { super(0); } }` would index `Leaf` with a one-line body range, so the `super(0)` call-site fell outside the Leaf class and no ctor body was recognized, silently dropping the `super(...)` chain edge from `callers` / `references` / `impact` even with the depth-aware ReferenceExtractor header collector in place. The same `FindBraceRange` depth tracking now also honors block comments (`/* ... */`), line comments (`//`), string literals (`"..."`), and Rust / OCaml-style lifetime annotations (`'a`, `'static`) separately from real single-character literals (`'x'`, `'\n'`), so unbalanced `(`, `[`, `{`, or `}` tokens living inside comments or strings can no longer break the body range.
